Strategic Interpretation

Yunavaun Tribe’s adaptive forest approach won because treasury, not territory, decided the ring: it finished with 208 against 147 even while trailing 11 regions to 13, so the larger map presence of the runner-up did not convert into the decisive resource edge. After a contested opening and midgame, Yunavaun Tribe’s early and mid economic shifts created the treasury lead that became central to the finish, which meant later territorial swings could not overturn the income gap. Yunavaun Field Rebels’ expansionist pressure mattered because it produced the region lead, but it failed to translate that board control into enough treasury to catch up.
The closest challenger was Yunavaun Field Rebels (Adaptive Coast) at 147 treasury and 13 regions.

Victor's History

The Yunavaun Tribe prevailed not by chasing the widest map share, but by building the stronger treasury and holding its course to the end. Its Adaptive Forest approach, shaped by geography, proved steadier than the more expansive claims of the Yunavaun Field Rebels, who at one point led in regions yet finished behind on treasury and rank. The decisive shifts in the early and mid game established a margin that the Tribe preserved through the final turns, and by turn 100 it stood first with 208 treasury and 11 regions. In this result, prudence and economic discipline mattered more than temporary breadth, and the Tribe’s coherence was rewarded accordingly.
